      This polymerized dopamine forms by a spontaneous oxidation reaction, and is formally a type of
      <a href="/wiki/Melanin" title="Melanin">
       melanin
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lynge_97-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lynge-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Synthesis usually involves reaction of dopamine hydrochloride with
      <a href="/wiki/Tris" title="Tris">
       Tris
      </a>
      as a base in water. The structure of polydopamine is unknown.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dreyer_96-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Dreyer-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Polydopamine coatings can form on objects ranging in size from nanoparticles to large surfaces. Polydopamine layers have chemical properties that have the potential to be extremely useful, and numerous studies have examined their possible applications. At the simplest level, they can be used for protection against damage by light, or to form capsules for drug delivery. At a more sophisticated level, their adhesive properties may make them useful as substrates for biosensors or other biologically active macromolecules.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lynge_97-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lynge-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dopamine&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_catecholamine_research" title="History of catecholamine research">
       History of catecholamine research
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Dopamine was first synthesized in 1910 by
      <a href="/wiki/George_Barger" title="George Barger">
       George Barger
      </a>
      and
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=James_Ewens&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="James Ewens (page does not exist)">
       James Ewens
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/Wellcome_Trust" title="Wellcome Trust">
       Wellcome
      </a>
      Laboratories in London, England
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and first identified in the human brain by
      <a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Montagu" title="Kathleen Montagu">
       Kathleen Montagu
      </a>
      in 1957. It was named dopamine because it is a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monoamine" title="Monoamine">
       monoamine
      </a>
      whose
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precursor_chemical" title="Precursor chemical">
       precursor
      </a>
      in the Barger-Ewens synthesis is 3,4-
      <i>
       d
      </i>
      ihydr
      <i>
       o
      </i>
      xy
      <i>
       p
      </i>
      henyl
      <i>
       a
      </i>
      lanine (levodopamine or
      <a href="/wiki/L-DOPA" title="L-DOPA">
       L-DOPA
      </a>
      ). Dopamine's function as a neurotransmitter was first recognized in 1958 by
      <a href="/wiki/Arvid_Carlsson" title="Arvid Carlsson">
       Arvid Carlsson
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Nils-%C3%85ke_Hillarp" title="Nils-ke Hillarp">
       Nils-ke Hillarp
      </a>
      at the Laboratory for Chemical Pharmacology of the National Heart Institute of
      <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">
       Sweden
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid11165672_99-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-pmid11165672-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Carlsson was awarded the 2000
      <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">
       Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine
      </a>
      for showing that dopamine is not only a precursor of
      <a href="/wiki/Norepinephrine" title="Norepinephrine">
       norepinephrine
      </a>
      (noradrenaline) and
      <a href="/wiki/Epinephrine" title="Epinephrine">
       epinephrine
      </a>
      (adrenaline), but also a neurotransmitter.
     </p>

          <a class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.1016%2Fj.tins.2007.03.006" rel="nofollow">
           10.1016/j.tins.2007.03.006
          </a>
          .
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">
           PMID
          </a>
          <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/17408759" rel="nofollow">
           17408759
          </a>
          .
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADopamine&amp;rft.atitle=Dopamine+neuron+systems+in+the+brain%3A+an+update&amp;rft.au=Bj%C3%B6rklund+A%2C+Dunnett+SB&amp;rft.aulast=Bj%C3%B6rklund+A%2C+Dunnett+SB&amp;rft.date=May+2007&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1016%2Fj.tins.2007.03.006&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F17408759&amp;rft.issue=5&amp;rft.jtitle=Trends+Neurosci.&amp;rft.pages=194-202&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=30">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-Malenka_pathways-6">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         ^
         <a href="#cite_ref-Malenka_pathways_6-0">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             a
            </b>
           </i>
          </sup>
         </a>
         <a href="#cite_ref-Malenka_pathways_6-1">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             b
            </b>
           </i>
          </sup>
         </a>
         <a href="#cite_ref-Malenka_pathways_6-2">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             c
            </b>
           </i>
          </sup>
         </a>
         <a href="#cite_ref-Malenka_pathways_6-3">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             d
            </b>
           </i>
          </sup>
         </a>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation book">
          Malenka RC, Nestler EJ, Hyman SE (2009). "Chapter 6: Widely Projecting Systems: Monoamines, Acetylcholine, and Orexin". In Sydor A, Brown RY.
          <i>
           Molecular Neuropharmacology: A Foundation for Clinical Neuroscience
          </i>
          (2nd ed.). New York: McGraw-Hill Medical. pp.147148, 154157.
          <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
           ISBN
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780071481274" title="Special:BookSources/9780071481274">
           9780071481274
          </a>
          .
          <q>
           Neurons from the
           <abbr title="Substantia nigra pars compacta">
            SNc
           </abbr>
           densely innervate the dorsal striatum where they play a critical role in the learning and execution of motor programs. Neurons from the
           <abbr title="Ventral tegmental area">
            VTA
           </abbr>
           innervate the ventral striatum (nucleus accumbens), olfactory bulb, amygdala, hippocampus, orbital and medial prefrontal cortex, and cingulate cortex. VTA
           <abbr title="Dopamine">
            DA
           </abbr>
           neurons play a critical role in motivation, reward-related behavior, attention, and multiple forms of memory.... Thus, acting in diverse terminal fields, dopamine confers motivational salience ("wanting") on the reward itself or associated cues (nucleus accumbens shell region), updates the value placed on different goals in light of this new experience (orbital prefrontal cortex), helps consolidate multiple forms of memory (amygdala and hippocampus), and encodes new motor programs that will facilitate obtaining this reward in the future (nucleus accumbens core region and dorsal striatum)....
           <abbr title="Dopamine">
            DA
           </abbr>
           has multiple actions in the prefrontal cortex. It promotes the "cognitive control" of behavior: the selection and successful monitoring of behavior to facilitate attainment of chosen goals. Aspects of cognitive control in which DA plays a role include working memory, the ability to hold information "on line" in order to guide actions, suppression of prepotent behaviors that compete with goal-directed actions, and control of attention and thus the ability to overcome distractions.... Noradrenergic projections from the
           <abbr title="locus coeruleus">
            LC
           </abbr>
           thus interact with dopaminergic projections from the VTA to regulate cognitive control....
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADopamine&amp;rft.atitle=Chapter+6%3A+Widely+Projecting+Systems%3A+Monoamines%2C+Acetylcholine%2C+and+Orexin&amp;rft.aulast=Malenka+RC%2C+Nestler+EJ%2C+Hyman+SE&amp;rft.au=Malenka+RC%2C+Nestler+EJ%2C+Hyman+SE&amp;rft.btitle=Molecular+Neuropharmacology%3A+A+Foundation+for+Clinical+Neuroscience&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.edition=2nd&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.isbn=9780071481274&amp;rft.pages=147-148%2C+154-157&amp;rft.place=New+York&amp;rft.pub=McGraw-Hill+Medical&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">

       <li id="cite_note-Nestler-45">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         ^
         <a href="#cite_ref-Nestler_45-0">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             a
            </b>

         </a>
         <a href="#cite_ref-Nestler_45-7">
          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             h
            </b>
           </i>
          </sup>
         </a>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation journal">
          Nestler EJ (December 2012).
          <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3569166" rel="nofollow">
           "Transcriptional mechanisms of drug addiction"
          </a>
          .
          <i>
           Clin. Psychopharmacol. Neurosci.
          </i>
          <b>
           10
          </b>
          (3): 136143.
          <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">
           doi
          </a>
          :
          <a class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.9758%2Fcpn.2012.10.3.136" rel="nofollow">
           10.9758/cpn.2012.10.3.136
          </a>
          .
          <a href="/wiki/PubMed_Central" title="PubMed Central">
           PMC
          </a>
          <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3569166" rel="nofollow">
           3569166
          </a>
          .
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PubMed_Identifier" title="PubMed Identifier">
           PMID
          </a>
          <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/23430970" rel="nofollow">
           23430970
          </a>
          .
          <q>
           FosB has been linked directly to several addiction-related behaviors... Importantly, genetic or viral overexpression of JunD, a dominant negative mutant of JunD which antagonizes FosB- and other AP-1-mediated transcriptional activity, in the NAc or OFC blocks these key effects of drug exposure14,2224. This indicates that FosB is both necessary and sufficient for many of the changes wrought in the brain by chronic drug exposure. FosB is also induced in D1-type NAc MSNs by chronic consumption of several natural rewards, including sucrose, high fat food, sex, wheel running, where it promotes that consumption14,2630. This implicates FosB in the regulation of natural rewards under normal conditions and perhaps during pathological addictive-like states.
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADopamine&amp;rft.atitle=Transcriptional+mechanisms+of+drug+addiction&amp;rft.aulast=Nestler+EJ&amp;rft.au=Nestler+EJ&amp;rft.date=December+2012&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC3569166&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.9758%2Fcpn.2012.10.3.136&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmc%2F3569166&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F23430970&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.jtitle=Clin.+Psychopharmacol.+Neurosci.&amp;rft.pages=136-143&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=10">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-Malenka_2009_04-46">
